Ticket: PFT-3801
Issue id: 183771
Module: Data & Reporting
Summary: DfE Assessment Excel Download Facility for Maintained Schools (as required by the DfE and LEA)
Role: School Business Manager
Source: June 2025 - Row 857
Comment: Currently you can only download a CTF to transfer DfE Statutory Assessments.

As a maintained school, we have to report the data to the LEA on an excel spreadsheet (created by the DfE for this purpose) so they can check and upload it to the DfE for all their schools, and we can't easily do this in Arbor.

Currently we have to download the data from the assessment page, then run a custom report to get the other fields, and then copy and paste from these two sheets into the DfE spreadsheet. This is not only time consuming, but also open to human error

This is the website where you can find the information for the EYFSP: https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/early-years-foundation-stage-profile-return/early-years-foundation-stage-profile-return-guide

And this is the one for Phonics: https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/phonics-screening-check-data-collection-guide/phonics-screening-check-data-collection-guide-2025#reporting-arrangements

There are probably similar ones for KS2 and above that you can find on the DfE website.

Ticket: PFT-3508
Issue id: 182845
Module: Attendance
Summary: Statutory attendance widget should not include Year 11 for second half of Summer Attendance
Role: Head of Data, Insight and Analysis
Source: June 2025 - Row 1150
Comment: Afternoon!

Summer Half Term Year 11 data shouldn't be reported in the widget for statutory attendance on the main school dashboard. This guidance can be found in the DfE methodology here: https://explore-education-statistics.service.gov.uk/methodology/pupil-absence-statistics-methodology (Data Collection section, under section 4.4.1 > Summer half term) - which explains that Year 11 data is collected but not reported.

Seeing the numbers in Arbor puts a perverse incentive on our staff to fiddle the figures to make them better, e.g. off-rolling pupils early, or recording them as B or # when they should really be S.

It would be amazing if you could align the Statutory widget with DfE methodology for Year 11. Thank you!

Ticket: PFT-3290
Issue id: 182304
Module: Behaviour
Summary: Detention allocation
Role: Deputy Headteacher
Source: June 2025 - Row 1368
Comment: Suggested Improvement: Automatic Sanctions in Behaviour Workflows

It would be extremely helpful if, as part of the behaviour workflow setup, schools could automatically schedule a sanction (e.g. detention) when a student reaches a defined number of incidents for a particular behaviour type.

Many schools issue detentions for repeated minor behaviours (such as incorrect uniform or missed homework). Currently, this can only be managed by creating a separate "detention" workflow that other workflows escalate to after a certain number of incidents. However, this approach means that each type of detention (e.g. lunchtime, after-school, subject-specific) requires its own dedicated workflow.

Since Arbor currently allows a maximum of five behaviour workflows, using several for detention allocation severely limits a school’s ability to create other useful workflows for different behaviour types.

A more flexible system that allows automatic sanction scheduling within a single workflow – triggered by behaviour frequency thresholds – would make this much more efficient and allow schools to manage behaviour escalation without compromising workflow capacity.

---

Ticket: PFT-3266
Issue id: 182191
Module: Medical
Summary: Accident Reporting - On App
Role: Admin
Source: June 2025 - Row 1392
Comment: Overview:
Introduce a dedicated Accident Reporting feature within the parent app that allows staff to quickly log incidents (e.g., trips, falls, cuts), record any first aid applied, and automatically notify parents/guardians in real time.

Why This Feature?
Critical for SEN Schools: These settings require rigorous, transparent, and timely communication around student well-being. A centralised digital record is invaluable.

Saves Time: Eliminates the need for paper forms or multiple communication steps.

Increased Parent Trust: Parents stay informed immediately and can review full details at their convenience.

Audit Trail: Provides a searchable history of incidents, including timestamps and staff involved—useful for both internal review and external reporting.

Key Functionalities:
Quick Logging Interface for Staff

Type of incident (trip, fall, bump, cut, etc.)

Time & location

Action taken (e.g., first aid, ice pack, monitored)

Optional notes or photo upload (e.g., minor scrape, playground location)

Auto-Notification to Parents

Instant in-app push notification

Summary view + full report available in the app

Parent View

Timeline of incident

What happened, what action was taken, by whom

Acknowledgement button (optional)

Admin Dashboard

Filter by date, student, incident type

Export reports (e.g., for school health & safety logs)

Benefits:
Enhances child safety protocols

Reduces admin burden

Builds trust with parents

Supports legal and safeguarding compliance

Source: June 2025 - Row 1483

These are children who have a diagnosed need that can be met within the universal provision within the classroom but this needs to be flagged to staff so that they are aware e.g. the children may have a Hearing Impairment or a diagnosis of ADHD or slow processing.
We are not 'monitoring' this child as we know what their identified need is to it would not be appropriate to use this category. This category would therefore default to the DfE's 'N' category.
These needs are not necessarily a medical need/diagnosis so it is therefore not appropriate to put them within this category either and the staff need this information within the SEN overview of their class so that they can plan to meet needs.
I have previously been able to add a new SEN Need Category in this way (defaulting to the appropriate DfE census category) to both Bromcom and SIMs and can't understand why I'm not able to do this within Arbor as it's extremely useful to staff and reassuring to parents for them to know that this information is accurately recorded and shared with staff.

Ticket: PFT-3111
Issue id: 181711
Module: Core Student Record
Summary: Suggestion for System Enhancement – Address Handling for Pupils with Split Residency
Role: Senior Office Manager
Source: June 2025 - Row 1547
Comment: I wanted to highlight an issue we experienced today that I believe could be addressed with a small but important enhancement to your system.

We encountered a problem with Birmingham LA only picking up the most recently added address for a pupil. In this case, the child lives equally between both separated parents, each residing in a different county. Unfortunately, the system’s default to the latest address caused a significant issue with the secondary school allocation — the new address being in a different county jeopardised the offer the pupil had been given.

To try and resolve the situation, I manually adjusted the "moved in" dates on the addresses so they reflect the correct shared residency, but I am concerned this workaround may have implications for the allocation process.

It would be very helpful if the system could be improved to more accurately reflect joint residency scenarios — perhaps by allowing both addresses to be flagged as equally valid "home" addresses, or by enabling clearer priority settings when a child lives 50/50 with both parents.
 Thank you for your continued support.

Ticket: PFT-3027
Issue id: 181449
Module: Groups & Enrolments
Summary: Umbrella method for setting up clubs
Role: Data Manager
Source: June 2025 - Row 1631
Comment: This is my issue:

I wanted to enquire whether anyone has found an effective way to structure clubs within School > Activities > Clubs using an umbrella approach—similar to the way courses are set up, where each course encompasses multiple forms.

At present, I’m finding it challenging to create a clear ‘parent’ club structure. This results in an overwhelming number of individual clubs, which skews reporting and analysis. For instance, it becomes difficult to determine which clubs are most popular among specific groups such as gender, year groups, or other demographic segments, as some clubs are run on a weekly / termly basis.

Any guidance or suggestions would be greatly appreciated.

This is Arbor HQ Member response:

Michaela Bassi
🚀
3h

Data Manager
I think it would be difficult to structure clubs - if they are anything like ours they are random depending on what the staff members interests are! We have 74 clubs which include Jiu Jitsu, Crocheting, Debating, Robotics and all the sports clubs! I also include Sports Fixtures as part of the Club module and preclude them all with Squad (i.e. Squad - Senior Athletics) just so I can separate them out. This is our first year using Arbor clubs and am still trying to figure out how to analyse it myself!

This is my response:

Mmmm…. we seem to have similar number of clubs as you do. Indeed, the analytical part isn’t as smooth as it could be. For example, if we would have a parent club called ‘Squad’, then it would make more sense when analysing data from associated sub-clubs eg. Female Squad Team, Male Squad Team, Junior, Senior, etc.

Conclusion

I'm confident that clubs analytics could be improved just by offering a more structured approach. In the end, to analyse 100 clubs is more time consuming vs analysing 10 parent club data.

Ticket: PFT-3018
Issue id: 181405
Module: Attendance
Summary: Absent mark for the U code is causing a safeguarding issue - it should show on registers as a late clock
Role: Samantha Keys-Kidd - Attendance Manager
Source: June 2025 - Row 1640
Comment: I can confirm that when a student is marked with a U code (Late after register closes), the Recent Changes section will show them as ❌ (absent). This is because, statistically and legally, all instances of the U code are classified as unauthorised absences.

When our teachers are taking the registers, we have noticed that if a child arrives late to school after registers have closed 'U' code, they have NOT been putting on a truancy ,as on the register, it appears that they are absent with a  ❌

We would suggest that although the U code is an absent mark, they are technically late, therefore, this would be better reflected for the teachers as a  LATE CLOCK  (like the 'L' code) so teachers know they have arrived late, and that they ARE in school ensuing that if they have truanted the lesson, they will be picked up for this and sanctions are put in place.
